Silk and Tea: New Information on Tea Markets in Zhejiang and Jiangxi 279

Suian: The green tea of Suichun has been selling well in recent years due to strong sales both to foreign and domestic merchants. Business is still considered decent. Last year, the offered price even increased to 94 yuan per dan. This year, the local mountain producers are deeply concerned that tea sales may be sluggish, so they are generally harvesting early to prevent price drops. If the weather turns favorable in the coming days, tea plucking and processing will begin. The number of tea firms setting up in the various villages is about the same as last year. However, the policy of each firm is to reduce mountain prices first to lower costs, taking that as the fundamental requirement, to avoid a repeat of the crisis as the overseas market price has not yet returned to a good state. Whether the mountain price can be lowered will depend on whether the trend in Hangzhou and Shanghai domestic markets is active or sluggish.

Xiushui: The black tea of Xiushui used to have prosperous business. In the last ten years, due to the deteriorating soil quality and the lack of cultivation by mountain producers, the tea leaf production has been poor, leading to a sharp decline in trade with foreign merchants. Production has also decreased significantly compared to the past. The year before last, there were still more than ten firms such as Zhongxin Chang that went into the mountains to provide funds for the black tea business. Because it was difficult to make a profit, the number of firms decreased again last year compared to the year before. According to Xunxun, it is said that the number of foreign firms setting up shop for black tea in the area this year is still uncertain. Generally, due to the tight credit, many are taking a wait-and-see approach. In the future, the number of those who proceed with the tea business will be small. However, smaller merchants and peddlers have already entered the mountains to collect raw tea leaves. The market is even more sluggish than before.

Fuliang: Fuliang tea leaves are divided into red and green tea. This year, tea trees in the eastern and southern villages have had slower bud development due to rainy and cold weather. As of this week, the early tea in Zhouyuan, Qingzui [place names], has begun to bud. Yesterday and today, the weather has cleared up and turned warmer, and the tea is ready for plucking. Mountain producers in various villages believe that local firms have decreased significantly this year, sales are sluggish, and market prices are naturally lower than before. The new prices for Mao Feng green tea at local shops are selling for 70-80 yuan per dan, so most producers are selling directly to the shops to get a good price. If the weather remains clear and rainless, new Mao Feng products will soon be available on the market.

Sunny and Warm Weather Brings a Turning Point for Zhejiang Sericulture 280

Xiaoshi is a well-known silk reeling area in Zhejiang province. Silk shops and silk trading firms are everywhere. Farmers all plant mulberry trees and raise silkworms as important agricultural activities. Every spring silkworm season, the mulberry fields are as lush and green as clouds. This year, the weather was cold, and mulberry trees sprouted slowly. Coupled with the rural economic panic, the silkworm season was late, and raising silkworms was not prosperous. Most of those who hatched native silkworm eggs feared the early silkworm season would follow last year's pattern, and most leaves were left to cold rain. Therefore, everyone raised late silkworms to compensate. After collecting the silkworm ants, the weather was still cold, alternating between sunny and rainy, and the silkworm ants did not develop well. Occasionally, some raised improved breeds. But when the weather turned sunny, with gentle breezes and warm sunshine, the silkworm ants thrived. However, the silkworm seasons varied: early silkworms had already undergone three molts and were consuming leaves, the next group had undergone two molts and had consumed leaves for four or five days, and the late silkworms had only undergone their first molt. The current situation is quite good, and sericulture can still be salvaged.

Deqing is also a major sericulture producing area in Huzhou. However, in recent years, farmers have been very discouraged due to repeated failures in raising silkworms. This year, Zhejiang is providing subsidies to encourage sericulture. Therefore, farmers who plant mulberry trees in Donghengli, Xintang Township, Dama Township, and other places are engaged in hatching silkworms. However, due to abnormal weather conditions, the climate was winter-like, and the mulberry trees produced leaves later, making the silkworm season also later. In the Xiagao and Xu areas, only 30-40% of the native silkworm eggs hatched due to the cold and rain. The later batches of foreign silkworms hatched in Xintang and other places have recently seen good weather and have been harvested completely. Currently, the early batches have been consuming leaves for five or six days, and the late batches have just begun to try leaves. Development is still good.

Silent Silk Market Due to Overcast Weather 281

Yesterday, the silk market was unusually quiet. Although New York rose by two points and Yokohama rose by twenty yuan, transactions were scarce. The reason for this is that, firstly, overseas customers are also uncertain about the silk market and are currently in a wait-and-see mode. Secondly, Shanghai exporters are finding that the quality of the spot goods they purchase often varies, making it difficult to judge. Reuters' silk market report stated that demand for spot transactions in New York was still strong last week, but transactions were slow. Furthermore, silk purchased at low prices previously has reappeared on the market. This week, silk prices rose by 2.5 to 5 cents per yard, but some goods did not increase in price. The appetite of crepe manufacturers is not large, but retail crepe de chine is still considered decent. The silk market at the exchange is still good, and artificial silk prices have also risen slightly. The prices in overseas markets are as follows (27th):

Free Talk

Civilization and Humanity 291

— Da Wu

It is said that we are now in a civilized world, and humans are civilized. For example, Europeans and Americans often pride themselves on being from civilized countries, while upper-class Chinese people and civilized gentlemen often scold those "uncivilized" lower-class Chinese as "barbarians." "Barbarian" happens to be the opposite of "civilized."

Civilization means things that make humans enjoy blessings, such as Ford airplanes or Cadillac cars, which are extremely convenient. In addition, there are wool, silk, and cotton clothes, as well as patriotic silk, free spinning, and (September 18th Incident) crepe: food includes Chinese and Western cuisine, delicacies from the sea and mountains; housing includes Chinese, Western, Roman, or Eastern styles, stone or cement buildings: Although humans cannot universally enjoy the blessings of civilization, civilization has already penetrated everywhere: some people are suffering from civilization, but some are enjoying the blessings of civilization. Therefore, some people, after making a living, still "play mahjong," fill out "liberation lyrics," or watch fat-bottomed sexy dances to celebrate the success of this civilization.

However, since civilized people scold uncivilized people as "barbarians," this reveals a bit of information: "barbarism" still exists alongside "civilization." Let's take a random example:

Not long ago, a friend was fortunate enough to be released from prison. He said that as soon as he entered the prison, he would be interrogated as usual. During the interrogation, torture would be used, such as sitting on a tiger bench or having tap water poured into his nostrils. He didn't know how others felt when they were tortured, but after he himself was tortured, he didn't feel much pain. He just carefully examined those who interrogated and tortured him for a long time. He always felt something was different and couldn't believe that they were the same human beings as himself. He suspected that they were another kind of fierce beast; but after repeatedly identifying them, they all had the appearance of human beings and wore human clothes. So he began to be surprised at how cruel humans could be to their own kind and how "barbaric" the world still was.

He entered the prison with this strange feeling and met the prisoners who were detained like him. At first, he was wary of them, because the people who maintained the law were already so cruel, so the lawbreakers must be even worse. Then he saw that they treated him as kindly as they would treat their own family members, and he couldn't help but be suspicious, and his previous feelings began to waver. This made him feel that humans were really "civilized" and approachable. However, as soon as he touched the wounds on his body and felt the pain, he felt that humans were "barbaric" again.

In fact, this is not difficult to understand; humans are originally civilized, but when they are opposed to each other, they become "barbaric."

However, this clearly shows the existence of "barbarism," which is exactly the opposite of "civilization."

Whether or not something is civilized depends on how humans use it to live their lives. This means is nothing more than treating nature and treating one's fellow humans. The former civilization has already brought some happiness to mankind, but the latter is still causing people to suffer, and is still "barbaric."

Water is flowing, and the ships floating on the water are also flowing. If the ship suddenly stops moving, it must have hit a reef or run aground on a beach. So what is it that is hindering half of human civilization?

However, I am not a Christian or a humanitarian, and I have no thought of "humanity" that would inspire me to say this; because, as long as the barbarism and cruelty of mankind are eliminated, even if it means using barbaric and cruel means, I will not regret it at all. Whether it's a donation for saving the country or a donation for aviation, I have generously given.

Humans are already half civilized, and that is in their treatment of nature. If we could remove that half of barbarism towards our fellow humans, not only would civilization be able to universally benefit all living beings, but also the entire human race would be transformed from its original sphinx-like form. However, that is not something that can be explained clearly with reason first.

But I think this time will not be long.

Bitter Smiles, Groans, and Cries 292

— Ba Jin

To My Brother (Continued)

I have said things that I have not said, and I have done things that I have not done. And those words and deeds were all contrary to my thoughts. Some people have fabricated various strange stories about my life in tabloids. Some people have used me in (interviews) (impressions), etc., to turn me into someone like them, saying what they think. A short manuscript of mine that was created as a joke a few years ago was signed with my current name and appeared in a memorial publication in Nanyang. A short message I sent to a friend was published in the supplement of an XX organ newspaper. An old manuscript of mine was given by a friend as a gift to an editor. After my article was reprinted by a magazine, the title was changed and advertisements were placed everywhere, making some young friends suspect that I had received a huge fee from that magazine (you know I have never received a single penny from that magazine); during my travels, an editor sent me his work to ask for my criticism, and I faithfully wrote my opinion in a reply, but my letter was deleted and published in the magazine. A translation of mine was taken by a friend who returned from Nanyang to publish. I proofread it myself and negotiated the printing myself. After the book came out, he did not give me a single penny in royalties or pay a single penny in printing costs. Instead, he scolded me behind my back for being stingy with him. Helping him resulted in his bookstore closing down, and the translation fell into the hands of another bookstore editor. That editor wanted me to sell it to him, and for the sake of several friends, I agreed. But now, a year after this small book was published, that editor is taking it to other bookstores to sell, and he is also spreading rumors that I owe him money and have not paid it back, and that I am using the translation as collateral. (There are many more things like this. In this literary world, in this publishing world, there are many things that make a real person bitter, groan, and I don't have time to tell you all of them.) I saw a person say a few words, and so this person connected my words and deeds with him or her and spread them out. I hate all the old bones covered by the name of Eastern culture, but others insist on sending me old poems, while thinking that they understand me very well.

In this way, I have become a tool for young ladies and gentlemen to play with. Not only have my words and deeds been raped, but my thoughts have also been raped several times. My thoughts are the things I cherish most! But others even want to take away this little bit of freedom of thought! But I have not issued a protest in the past two years. I just smile bitterly, I just groan. Because they say they are all my friends.

You don't know how much I hate my name now! Several times in sleepless nights, I violently grabbed my hair and violently beat my chest. Intense hatred tore at my heart, and boundless darkness surrounded me. At that time, I really hoped that there would be a force to destroy myself. I really cannot endure this kind of life anymore. I clearly love my articles, but now my articles have been ruined to the point that I have to hate them. This situation is like a mother seeing her child being ravaged and losing its human form. You should understand that pain too.

Now, no matter what, I should end my past life. In order to be a real and brave person, in order to be loyal to my own beliefs, in order to prevent the day when I would personally cut off my own life, I should stay away from those literati, I should throw myself into real life, and find strength in action, as I hoped in (The Cry of a Dying Soul). This is what I mean by (taking life as a desperate gamble).

Whether I will ever be able to break free from all the encirclement and be reborn, I myself do not know. But I am now

crying out. You are my only brother, and I hope that you will always remember me in danger and hardship and give me blessings! (The End)

In a Train in Berlin 293

— Wen Yuan

The train climbed out of Berlin. The train was full of women and children. There were almost no strong men. In one of the carriages, a gray-haired Landsturm soldier was sitting next to a weak, sick old woman. In the rumbling of the train wheels, passengers could hear her counting: (One, two, three,) clearly completely absorbed in her own thoughts. Every now and then, she repeated these numbers. Two girls giggled at this strange behavior, innocently talking about some unconscious things. An elder frowned and scolded them a few words, and then silence enveloped everything.

(One, two, three,) clearly unconsciously, this woman repeated, and the girls giggled again. At this time, the gray-haired Landsturm soldier leaned forward.

(Ladies,) he said seriously, (if I told you that this poor woman is my wife, I'm afraid you wouldn't laugh anymore. In the war, we lost our three sons. Now, before I go to the front myself, I have to send their mother to an insane asylum.)

The carriage instantly became terribly silent.

(Translated from the Irish O. ERoilly)

Random Words from Everywhere 294

— Zi Zhan

(22) Memorial to the Emperor by Examination Candidates

Kang Youwei traveled to the capital five times and submitted memorials to the emperor seven times, but it was the memorial by examination candidates that most shocked the world. He once wrote a poem to commemorate the event, saying, "The Eastern affair was defeated, and I united three thousand examination candidates from eighteen provinces to submit a memorial. The next day, the American envoy Denby requested the draft, which was copied and engraved all over the world, titled 'Record of the Memorial to the Emperor by Examination Candidates.'" At that time, the main advocate for peace was Grand Councilor Sun Yujun, who incurred great public anger. Sun, fearing to attend court, resigned his position. The poem says:

The sea dragon weeps as ships sink in the waves,

The senior minister goes out in a light carriage to discuss peace,

The Liaodong territory is about to be carved up and handed over.

Many examination candidates lay prostrate before the palace gates to protest,

Three thousand people signed their names, their carriage wheels rubbing together,

A convoy of five miles blocked the streets.

The Taiwanese people weep and sing of Qin Hui,

Spies and rumors spread throughout the nine cities.

Carrying coffins and clenching fists, they beat the drums three times.

Qin Hui avoids the court, fearing rebuke.

The American envoy Denby is amazed by the morale of the scholars!

He requests the draft to copy and spread, ink vying to be ground all over the world.

Alas! What to do if we cannot smash Qin!

Reading this poem, we can imagine the scale of the movement to petition the emperor and how vigilant the government was. The fact that the prime minister was willing to take responsibility and resign shows that there was still something called "public opinion" at that time. Previously, when the telegram reporting that the peace treaty with Japan, consisting of eleven articles, had been signed by a plenipotentiary official arrived in Beijing, the whole country was in an uproar. Both officials within the central government and local officials outside the capital had arguments. The most vocal and激烈的發言激動者 who spoke out most vehemently were the examination candidates. After completing the examination in the Ministry of Rites, they beat the Dengwen Drum and competed to submit memorials. Initially, more than a hundred Guangdong examination candidates, including Liang Qichao, and dozens of Hunan examination candidates, including Ren Xichun, Wen Junduo, and Tan Shaochang, first went to the Censorate to request that they submit the memorial on their behalf. Then, the provinces of Fujian, Sichuan, Jiangxi, and Guizhou followed. Then, the provinces of Jiangsu, Hubei, Shaanxi, Gansu, and Guangxi followed. Then, the provinces of Zhili, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, and Yunnan followed. From February 28, 30, April 2, 4, 6, etc., on the days when the Censorate held its bi-daily court sessions, the outside of the gate was filled with the clamor of carriages and horses, officials in their robes mingled together, the discussions were heated, and the shouting reverberated through the sky. After several days of not receiving a response to the memorials, the examination candidates from various provinces united again and submitted another memorial, with Guangdong examination candidate Kang Youwei (Zuyi) in charge. The memorial was long (more than eighteen thousand words), beginning with "We, examination candidates Kang Zuyi, etc., submit this memorial concerning matters of national safety, requesting that a clear decree be issued, with great rewards and punishments, to move the capital, train troops, and reform the laws, in order to block the peace agreement and resist foreign barbarians, protect our territory, and extend the life of the nation, requesting that you submit this memorial on our behalf." It stated that the Emperor should issue a decree to boost the morale of the nation, move the capital to establish the foundation of the nation, train troops to strengthen the power of the nation, and reform the laws to achieve good governance of the nation. To boost the morale of the nation, they suggested issuing a decree of self-reproach, a decree of clear punishment, and a decree seeking talent. To establish the foundation of the nation, they suggested moving the capital to Chang'an. To strengthen the power of the nation, they suggested selecting generals, purchasing weapons, and organizing overseas Chinese troops. To achieve good governance of the nation, they suggested laws for enriching the nation, such as currency laws, railroads, machinery and steamships, mining, silver coinage, and postal services. They also suggested laws for nurturing the people, such as promoting agriculture, encouraging industry, providing for merchants, and caring for the poor. To care for the poor, they suggested resettlement, vocational training, and providing for the destitute. They also suggested laws for educating the people, such as dividing the civil service examination into literary and artistic subjects and abolishing military subjects, establishing libraries everywhere, encouraging newspapers, and promoting morality. Finally, they suggested laws for reforming the political system, such as reducing redundant officials, decreasing stipends, storing up talent, sending students abroad, selecting advisory officials, and recruiting civilian soldiers. They concluded by saying that if everything were renewed and we used the land of two million square miles, the four hundred million people, and the two hundred and sixty thousand kinds of products to strive for self-strengthening, then this would be a great worry for Japan and a secret concern for the countries of Europe. If we hesitate, delay, muddle along, cling to the old ways, and miss the opportunity, then the various foreign powers will surround us, leaving no room for escape, and even a sage would be unable to improve the situation. After the draft was completed, it was circulated for discussion at the Jiancao Hall in the Songjun Hermitage south of Xuanwu City, the former residence of the Ming official Yang Jiaoshan. The peace agreement was originally scheduled to be exchanged in Yantai on April 14, so the official memorial was also scheduled to be submitted to the Censorate on the 10th, with the 7th, 8th, and 9th being the dates for the meeting. However, the envoy who negotiated the peace and the minister who advocated for it, fearing that public sentiment would be turbulent and the situation would change, hastily requested on the 8th that the peace agreement be sealed and sent with the envoy. Alas, the memorial was not submitted, but the agreement was already finalized, and it was only seen that this grand document was copied and engraved all over the world. What was the point?

Carrot Hair 295

— Written by Jules Renard, Translated by Lin Qu

Rabbit

"(There's no watermelon left for you,)" Mrs. Lepic said; "(Actually, you're like me, you don't like watermelon.)" "(Of course,)" Carrot Hair thought.

His tastes were completely arranged by others. Generally speaking, he could only take his mother's tastes as his own. When eating cheese:

"(I believe Carrot Hair definitely won't eat it,)" Mrs. Lepic said.

"(Since she believes I definitely won't eat it, there's no need to try it.)"

Besides, he knew it was dangerous.

But even if he didn't try it, didn't he have a chance to satisfy his quirks in a place only he knew? When the last dish of the meal was served, Mrs. Lepic said to him:

"(Take these few slices of eaten watermelon to your rabbits.)"

Carrot Hair slowly walked to do the chore, holding the plate level, so as not to spill the contents.

When he walked into the rabbit's hutch, the rabbits were so happy that they jumped around, their ears stood up high, their noses facing the sky, their front feet stretched straight, as if preparing to beat a drum, everyone crowded around him.

"(Ah! Wait a minute, Carrot Hair said;)" (Slow down a bit, let's all share.)"

He sat on a pile of dirt and wild chrysanthemum roots, cabbage heads, sunflower leaves and the like. He fed the watermelon seeds to the rabbits, and drank the melon juice himself: it was as sweet as sweet wine.

Afterwards, he scraped the sweet yellow pulp left over by the people at home with his teeth, eating everything that could still be dissolved, and then threw the green hard skin to the rabbits standing on their hind legs around him.

The door of the rabbit hutch was closed.

The midday sun, lazily leaking through the cracks in the tiles, dipped its tail of light in the cool shadows.

Aviation and Air Defense 296

— Xiao Zhi

Not long ago, I wrote something about (aviation to save the country), advocating that while everyone is shouting (donate money to buy airplanes), in addition to everyone should take out money (in fact, this is fundamentally impossible, but there is simply no way otherwise), we must also actively train flight and combat personnel, set up factories to manufacture airplanes, and explore for gasoline, because if these three problems are not solved first, then the throats of the people of the country will be hoarse, or even if the (bought) airplanes are so numerous that there is no place to put them, the (country) will still not be (saved), and it will also create a new and greater crisis,

But what is equally important as (aviation) and must also be arranged at the same time as (aviation) is (air defense). When we open the former Japanese newspapers, we find two news items about our enemies' air force on the second page,

(1) They are actively training for long-distance combat over a 5,000-kilometer round trip from Hamamatsu to Taiwan.

(2) Yoshihiro Yoshida, a retired soldier, has invented a precisely constructed (light anti-aircraft gun). It is reported that this new type of weapon has six gun barrels, and it automatically determines the standard for objects moving at high speeds such as airplanes and can fire freely.

From these two news items, we can see that the enemy is working hard on the offensive and defensive training and equipment for air combat. If we look around at the countries that have airplanes, there is no country that is not studying (air defense) plans, and no country that is not trying its best to (air defense) drills. But what about ourselves? (Just buying airplanes!) (Just buying airplanes!) It seems that as soon as an airplane is (bought), the (country) will not only be (saved) by this (purchase), but also the enemy planes will flee at the mere sight of us. May I ask how can such a flustered state be expressed in color, and how can it not give the enemy reason to laugh at me as an unorganized country?

Some people say that China does not need to use airplanes at all, because China has people who can (fly). Look, didn't the newspaper a few days ago, with fancy borders, say that a certain chairman is recruiting talents who can walk on walls? Above the (eaves and walls) one can (fly away), of course one can take to the air and fly; is not being able to fly in the air the same effect as an airplane? Therefore, the Chinese people do not need to spend money to buy airplanes from foreigners, and of course they do not need to talk about (air defense), because people are alive and agile, they can move at will in the air, and they can fly on the enemy's airplanes and cut off the enemy's wing blades with a (big knife) to make them ineffective. Isn't this much cleaner than so-called (air defense)! Therefore, it proves that the chairman's intentions are good,

However, this is ultimately nonsense, a joke of the world, but it can also be seen that the leisurely sentiments and uselessness of the Chinese people are incomparable to the enemy's scheming, insidious, and viciousness.

But empty talk about (aviation), or blindly (donating money to buy airplanes), its uselessness and leisurely sentiment are also likely to have the same wonderful effect, so I say,

(1) Rather than not train flight and combat personnel, it is better to simply give the (bought) airplanes to the enemy, lest we waste resources and be laughed at by the people of the world,

(2) Rather than not manufacture airplanes and gasoline ourselves, it is better for the people of the country to simply remit the money they are preparing to donate to foreign countries (to buy airplanes) to foreign countries to show respect to foreigners, lest a group of (enthusiastic to save the country) adults and gentlemen work hard and hurt their hearts,

(3) Without (air defense), one simply does not need to (aviation), and the (country) may simply not need to be (saved), otherwise it is equivalent to taking (bought) airplanes unconditionally to be a living target for the enemy's (light anti-aircraft guns), or honestly like young Marshal Zhang to generously give hundreds of airplanes to the enemy to paint them and bomb the lives and properties of our Chinese people,

Spring is Gone, National Calamity is Heavy, Sad Remembrance of World Affairs, Tears Wet My Blue Robe, Hence I Compose Two Ci Poems (Remembering the Prince) to Express My Sorrow 297

— Zhou Mingliang

For no reason, I feel the dust calamity drifting,

Shredded brocade and remnant silk fly all over the courtyard,

Rain and wind are unbearable to hear,

Tears are full,

The sound of the eaves horse in front of the window saddens me,

Day after day, the wind and rain are even more desolate,

The flower season is waning, the cold is about to stiffen,

Purple and red, who advocates for what,

My mind wanders,

Leaning obliquely against the curtain, my heart breaks.

Strive 298

— Kuang

"Strive" is such an inauspicious word. If one does not have the fortune to possess things on one's own, but can only rely on striving to find a way, then it is no wonder that the gentlemen of ancient times, the Buddhist monks who folded their hands and chanted "Amitabha," and the Lord Jesus, who said, "If someone strikes you on the left cheek, offer them the right also," have always despised and opposed it. Unexpectedly, those who love to strive come up with a plan, changing the appearance of the word, but its inner meaning remains the same. For example, "competing for supremacy," "chasing the deer," (:::) are all examples of this.

Striving is indeed not a threshold. Just look at the sighs of the ancients: "Fighting for land leads to war, killing fills the fields; fighting for a city leads to war, killing fills the city." Using striving to cause killing to fill (fields and cities), its crime is truly heinous. Therefore, philosophers who opposed striving emerged, creating philosophies that said: "Gentlemen value ritual, petty men value striving." In Western Europe, there was also such a sage, whom everyone probably knows, Prince Kropotkin, the founder of anarchism, who wrote a book called "Mutual Aid," strongly advocating the idea of non-striving. This book has long been translated in China. I remember that in Beijing there was once a solicitation for (Ten Essential Books for Young People), and some scholars and celebrities selected this "Mutual Aid." I don't know why, but it offended Mr. Marx, who seemed like a flood or a fierce beast, and he wrote a famous book called "The Poverty of Philosophy," which refuted Kropotkin's "Mutual Aid." He not only criticized Kropotkin's "Mutual Aid," but also thoroughly advocated class struggle, which is the ultimate form of striving.

Therefore, the word "strive" cannot be destroyed after all, and the way of striving becomes more widespread, and the facts of striving become ubiquitous.

If others bully me, I will not submit and will appeal to the court. When the court opens, there will inevitably be a (struggle to reason). Even now, when countries occasionally resort to arms, weaker countries, fearing confusion, also appeal to (international courts) (League of Nations). This not only requires (struggling to reason), but it is said that it also requires (struggling to uphold justice). If the arm is about to be broken! Qing Yong made

If one cannot win even in court, one can only bear the injustice and go to the public to struggle, like the case of the female fortune-teller Wen Ying, who was murdered. Her mother, dissatisfied with the court's verdict, carried an appeal to Beijing some time ago, petitioning various judicial organs, and it is said that it has been quite effective.

Extending this to the rich and powerful families (with food stretching a square foot in front of them and numerous concubines), the struggles between the wives and concubines for the husband often lead to torn clothes and pants, and even the sight of short knives, broken heads. There is indeed such a set of struggles between wives and concubines.

Extending this to two men chasing after one woman, or two women chasing after one man, there is inevitably a scene of (competing for superiority), and it is said that the element of striving is the strongest because the jealousy is too deep. Therefore, even someone as weak as Tao Sijin, in order to possess the writer Xu Qinwen, used a kitchen knife to cut off five inches of Liu Mengying's beautiful neck, causing herself to eat Si Guan even now.

Furthermore, there are men of letters and scholars who, when they are so poor that they have no way to praise themselves, will also come up with two or three sentences of (struggling for life) (the word "挣" originally came from the word "争") or a set of (struggling for freedom of speech), but these two are quite difficult to strive for.

Speaking of our noble country, people love to haggle over one or two copper coins with rickshaw pullers, often arguing until their faces are red and twitching, and they dare not give way even slightly.

In ancient times, there was (the snipe and the clam fought, and the fisherman benefited), and now the general military and politicians are playing this game in full swing. The four northeastern provinces may be occupied by Japanese soldiers, but internal strife cannot be stopped. One scene after another is being shown before our eyes. Often, after a period of internal strife, there will be a period of peace, and then another period of internal strife, cycling up and down, succeeding and generating each other, resulting in the current situation! The national fortune is declining day by day, and the people are living in poverty.

So, what is the way of striving? I say: In China, it is indeed only like this.

After Reading the (Public Notice for Pacifying the People) in Beiping 299

— Xu Yu

After the defeat in eastern Hebei, the people of Tianjin and Beiping were in a panic. The mayor of Beiping announced a public notice for pacifying the people, saying: (1) The Beiping Public Security Bureau has organized wartime police teams to strengthen vigilance and cooperate with the military to maintain public order. (2) Air defense facilities have been completed. Even if airplanes appear in the skies of Beiping, they will not be able to stay for a long time. (3) The Tianjin-Beiping Railway has been assigned round-the-clock vigilance by the railway police. The enemy's conspiracies will definitely not be realized, etc. (Actually copied from the late evening edition of the 20th of April) I wonder what the local common people thought after reading it?

I am someone who used to be a common person in Beiping, and every time the civil war came close to Tianjin and Beiping, I read similar notices. At first, I was very skeptical, thinking that if more than 100,000 troops could not resist the (enemy) (?), how could the police resist them? Therefore, my heart became even more (panicked).

I believe that my friends in Shanghai will definitely think that my question is reasonable, or when you read the notice in the newspaper, you had already asked this question before me.

You will definitely think that my question is reasonable, or Actually, later facts told me that this question was wrong.

I have experienced many times in Beiping during times of civil war (panic), so not long after, I knew the meaning of the notice. So, looking at those newly arrived residents who were (panicked) after reading the notice, I found it laughable. Because I had already changed from a small common person to an old common person, so that notice was indeed (pacifying me a lot).

Because experience told me that the situation was like this: the so-called (wartime police team) and the like, in addition to using a gun salute to send the A army out of the back door quietly, also had to use a gun salute to welcome the B army entering from the front door.

After the B army came in, everything was the same as before, except that there were some changes in the newspapers (a new emperor, a new dynasty), those police officers never changed.

The way to (panic) is originally about fearing stray bullets, robbery, and street fighting, so in this way, except for rich merchants who have to send some offerings to welcome and send off, the rest do not need to (panic) much.

Counting my (panicked) experiences, the most noteworthy was when the National Revolutionary Army marched north to Tianjin and Beiping; at that time, the so-called (panic) was still about (internal war) outside of the civil war.

At that time, Tianjin had Zhang Zongchang, and Beiping had Zhang Zuolin, who sent out 100,000 fierce (plainclothes detectives) to detect the so-called (plainclothes teams). At that time, the victory of the Northern Expeditionary Army relied heavily on (plainclothes teams), so expanding (plainclothes detectives) was indeed a way to fight poison with poison. However, (plainclothes teams) appeared and disappeared unpredictably, similar to (Communists), often hiding among young people, and entering and exiting the houses of universities, so we university students were particularly likely to be detected as (plainclothes teams) by (plainclothes detectives). So this (wartime plainclothes detective) was the most (panicked) thing, which was somewhat different from the (wartime police team).

But I still have to go back to the main topic. At that time, there was also a police team that (cooperated with the military). They were awe-inspiring and full of vigor, freely searching everywhere day and night. A house rented together by female students was searched by them many times at night. They must know more than I do, so I don't want to say much here.

But there was an obvious distinction between the crimes brought up by these two. No matter whether the evidence was a red silk scroll (don't laugh, this is a fact, it was once considered a red flag covering the ground), or a small publication sympathizing with the poor, or the Three Principles of the People, or the so-called speeches and will of the late premier; once it fell into the hands of the plainclothes detectives, it became a (plainclothes team), and once it fell into the hands of the (police team cooperating with the military), it immediately became a (Communist); but both were (sentenced to death), this was the same.

However, when the Northern Expeditionary Army entered the city, the first to hang the flag of the Blue Sky, White Sun, and Red Ground was the executive office that had executed people for hiding this kind of flag just the day before.

And the one using the Blue Sky White Sun hat badge was not the undying (plainclothes team), but the police who had executed the (plainclothes team).

Once, I even saw in the police station a police officer who had searched us many times and arrested my friend for hiding the Three Principles of the People, reading a teaching material on the Three Principles of the People; after inquiring, I learned that it was for the purpose of taking the (Party Ideology) exam, which made me suddenly realize everything!

However, all of this is completely different from this (wartime police team), but from this, one thing can be known, that is, their responsibility is not in resisting foreign aggression, but in maintaining public order. What is vigilantly guarded all night is not the (enemy country), but the (enemy country's conspiracies); the (enemy country's conspiracies) are the same as the former (plainclothes teams), that is, (traitors)!

Writing to this point, I suddenly thought of the suggestion in the newspaper that some people would fill Tianjin with a buffer zone. Therefore, the concept of a (buffer police team) could not help but make me (panic).

If it is really the same as what I saw several times during the previous civil wars, then this (public notice for pacifying the people) made me, a small common person in faraway Shanghai, (panic)!

Oh dear! Readers, please forgive me! I suddenly have a splitting headache, my eyes are dizzy, and I see them all taking out (fake flags), putting on (fake hat badges), and holding up (fake righteousness):::::! Forgive me for not being able to write more.

April 25, 1933.

Moving is Difficult 300

— Wu Yong

I remember when I was in my hometown, helping neighbors and relatives move, I often heard these words: "(It's really not easy for farmers to move! As the saying goes, 'Moving makes you poor for ten years.' This sentence is not wrong at all. When poor people move once, building a small shed costs thirty or twenty! People come to help, and you have to serve them food, which costs at least three or two dollars! Everything is expensive these days, but grain is worthless. Fixing this, fixing that, everywhere costs money! Where does this money come from? Doesn't it all come from those few catties of grain?)"

Yes, moving is really not easy, I understand that very well. Recently, after reading the reports in the newspapers about the Japanese army's atrocities in Rehe, it further proves the correctness of my theory. (::: Women committed suicide due to being raped by Japanese soldiers. Even more tragic was that several pregnant women were stabbed through their abdomens with guns by Japanese soldiers because the Chinese women refused to let the Japanese soldiers take their cattle and sheep. (Author's note: Of course, the children in their abdomens were also stabbed, that's all.)

The vast Chinese people, after suffering such atrocities, why don't they move? Of course, it is because moving is difficult, they don't have money to move, that's right. However, when talking about this, a small note should be added, which is: those who (seek the interests of the people) and those wealthy people who (run around for the country, risking their lives) are exceptions. Because their (responsibilities are great), they should preserve their lives. Because they want to preserve their lives, they have to move, and of course moving is not difficult for them.

When the Japanese army comes south, they move north (antiques, treasures, etc. go with them), when the Japanese army comes north, they move south, when the Japanese army comes east, they move west. Anyway, the Japanese army cannot come from the west, so they will not move to the East Sea, which is really a fortunate thing!

As for those with economic vision, of course, they spend ten million or five million in advance to set up private residences in foreign concessions, move their families there, which can save the trouble of moving back and forth, and can also avoid airplanes and all dangers, (preserve strength to prepare for resistance against Japan!) How wonderful! As for institutions and the like that are not convenient to set up in concessions, of course, it is a bit more troublesome to go back and forth, but in these days of convenient transportation, it doesn't matter much!

Apart from the unavoidable circumstances mentioned in the above small note, I still consistently maintain! Moving is very difficult, that's right! So we can only not move and really (resist Japan)!

A LETTER OF DIVORCE AND REMARRIAGE 301

— Nancun

Most people from the four districts of Guangdong venture far across the oceans to engage in commerce. Young men leave and return only when their hair is white. They prioritize profit over separation, often neglecting their wives. Occasionally, there are cases of wives secretly remarrying, which is truly lamentable. A certain Miss Mou from Tai County, born into a scholarly family, was quite literate. At the age of seventeen, she married the son of the Ouyang family in a neighboring village. Three days after their marriage, they separated for ten years. She was then seduced by a Mr. Ji and wrote a letter to her husband, divorcing him and remarrying. My friend, Mr. Ouyang, is a cousin of her former husband. He visited the family and sent me the original letter. I found the letter's wording and sentiments to be subtle and restrained, sad but not bitter, with the gentle and peaceful tone of a poet. I quickly transcribed it and submitted it to this column, hoping to warn those who prioritize profit over separation.

The letter says, "I have heard that Zhou Dynasty rituals have not changed, and a husband can remarry. Although the laws of the country are strict, they do not prohibit women from remarrying. Stay if you are compatible, leave if you are not. Marriage values freedom. Marrying again and again makes marriage seem like child's play. Therefore, though Huai Ying was of low status, she remarried Chong'er. Though Xia Shi was ill-fated, she remarried Wuchen. In ancient times, people valued etiquette and still could not remain married to one person until death. How much more so today, when people emphasize freedom. Why be surprised that people change their minds? Ask who in the world has ever kept a vow of chastity like the Cypress Boat? It is difficult for me to cherish youth like the willows by the roadside today. Moreover, you and I had only been married for three days before separating for ten years. My pillow is cold, my quilt is frigid, and I have long lived like a widow with a husband in name only. Time and things change, and I am left with a body waiting to die. Although there is the empty name of husband and wife, there is no joy of a family. If I wait twenty-five years to remarry, I will lament as I approach my coffin. I fear the decay of my beauty. The falling plums pass quickly, which is why I am so eager to leave and remarry. Fortunately, the old man under the moon is kind, and the red thread is tied again. A palace lady has intentions, and a red leaf is inscribed again. An old bride becomes a new bride. This is not my intention. A good couple turns into a resentful couple. How sad. However, Zhu Maichen was unable to support his wife and was forced to let her go. Shi Xiaoshu could not protect his wife and caused her to leave her husband. In the future, spilt water is difficult to recover, and I will part ways forever. After this, you will not see me in the palace. How can you feel anything for me? A parting gift. My thoughts carried on the wind. Please forgive me. I am endlessly agitated." I wonder if Mr. Ouyang felt anything when he read the letter.

TIME IN A DREAM (40 CONTINUED) 302

— Qin Shouou

Walking into a teahouse that also sold snacks, Wu Yi casually picked a seat, while Li Jinbiao first removed the stiff-brimmed police officer's hat from his head and straightened his clothes before sitting bolt upright on the square stool below Wu Yi.

(What exactly is going on)? After a round of tea, Wu Yi couldn't help but bring up the main topic.

(It's really a big joke)! Officer Li took a refined sip of black tea and said with a smile, (Principal Wu, I really don't understand why people's minds are always like this, why are they more clever than ghosts, and they can come up with all sorts of strange and cunning ideas! : : : )

(But, let's not: : :) Wu Yi heard him going on and on about empty theories, and hurriedly stopped him.

(Then let's talk about today's matter)! Li Jinbiao took another sip of tea. (Didn't the newspaper today publish a news item about a certain Xu Qiao? After our Director saw it, he became very suspicious: First, why didn't we hear about any kidnapping cases in the past few days; Second, Zhuangyuan Lane is a bustling area, and our Third District Fourth Precinct is located there. If something like that really happened, how would we save face? Third, no matter how fierce a certain foreigner is, he would never dare to make trouble in the capital; : : : He thought it didn't seem right, so he immediately summoned our Third District Chief Lin and told him to quickly send people to inquire in all directions, and be sure to find out the truth about this matter: : : :)

Wu Yi listened with fascination, holding an empty cup in his hand, not putting it down. Officer Li thought he wanted more tea, and hurriedly interrupted his words, picking up the teapot to pour for him.

(Don't bother! Don't bother! Tell me your story)! Wu Yi snatched the teapot and urged him to speak quickly.

(Our District Chief Lin didn't dare to neglect it, so he immediately went to the newspaper offices to inquire, asking them where the news came from. Everyone said it was sent by some correspondence. District Chief Lin hurried to the correspondence agency and saw that the correspondence agency was actually located together with the support association, and the president was that Xu Qiao. At that time, there was no one working inside, only two or three clerks left. District Chief Lin asked them where the Xu family's residence was. This question revealed the truth. Two or three people looked at each other, always hesitating and not speaking. District Chief Lin saw that the situation was not right, so he quickly called our Second District Sixth Precinct and told us to send a few brothers nearby. So I took three brothers to see him. He first told us to have one person guard the door and one person guard the telephone, not allowing them to communicate the news, and he himself tried his best to interrogate the three clerks, and after a while, one of them revealed the residence of Xu Qiao: : : .)

Li Jinbiao drank a cup of tea before continuing:

(District Chief Lin hired a car, took this clerk and the three of us, and rushed to Xu Qiao's house together; when we got there, it was lucky that Mr. Xu was just sitting in a bright and shiny car returning from outside: : : )

(Ah! Wasn't he injured)? Wu Yi thought this was too unreasonable, and hurriedly interrupted to ask.

(Don't interrupt me! Principal Wu! You'll understand when you hear the rest)! Li Jinbiao didn't answer Wu Yi's question first, but just told the facts. (Originally, neither District Chief Lin nor I knew him, but the clerk pointed him out. District Chief Lin saw that he was fat and big-eared, with red lips and white teeth, not to mention that he didn't look like he was covered in injuries or had walked forty or fifty miles, he was simply much stronger than us. He already understood half of it in his heart. When Mr. Xu saw that he had been led by his subordinates, he knew that he couldn't escape, so he put on a smiling face and hurriedly invited us in: : :

(After sitting down, he hurriedly offered tea and cigarettes, and was extremely polite. Then, he took out a large stack of banknotes from his pocket and smiled at District Chief Lin: (Old Brother), we are all people who make a living outside. Please keep this matter a secret for me: : : )
